## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The variables x (position), v (velocity), and dv_dt (acceleration) indicate a second-order ODE for an oscillator. In nonlinear oscillation models, dv_dt is typically composed of restoring-force terms depending on x, damping terms depending on v, and optional forcing/parametric terms depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force (simple harmonic oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations about equilibrium)
- Linear damping + linear restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscously damped oscillator)
- Constant bias / gravity-like offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (shifted equilibrium / constant external acceleration)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Pure nonlinear restoring (odd polynomial): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (symmetric nonlinear potential expansion)
- Pendulum-type restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (finite-angle pendulum with damping; non-polynomial restoring)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to speed squared)
- Cubic velocity damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation / empirical damping)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent pumping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (alternative self-excited oscillator form)
- Driven oscillator (harmonic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, bistability, chaos)
- Parametric stiffness modulation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance from time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear coupling between x and v: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (state-dependent damping / geometry-induced drag)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt depends only on x and is typically odd in x around equilibrium (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - c*x**3), reflecting dv_dt = -dU/dx for some potential U(x).
- Damping identification → terms proportional to v, v*Abs(v), or v**3 dissipate energy; increasing nonlinearity in v often models high-speed drag.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles → negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude is captured by factors like (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v.
- Finite-angle/periodic geometry → sin(c*x) restoring indicates angular variables or periodic potentials; small-x expansion recovers polynomial stiffness.
- External periodic drive → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms create resonance/entrainment; harmonics may appear if forcing is non-sinusoidal.
- Parametric excitation → time-modulating the x coefficient (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x) produces instability bands distinct from additive forcing.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → cubic stiffness (-c*x**3) produces hardening/softening behavior; structurally shows up as odd higher powers of x.
- Equilibrium shifts and asymmetry → constant terms or even powers of x in dv_dt suggest biased potentials or asymmetric restoring forces (equilibrium not at x=0).

4. `-3.05641*x` (linear in x)
5. `+0.26607*sin(t)` (sin(t) term)

The key basis functions are: `v`, `v*x²`, `x*|v|^(1/3)`, `x`, `sin(t)`.

The critical term is `x*|v|^(1/3)` — this involves the absolute value of v raised to 1/3 power. Any candidate that doesn't have a way to produce this term cannot match.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `|v|^(1/3)` or equivalent:

**Candidates 1-2, 6:** Have `sqrt(v+c)` terms — these produce `|v+c|^(1/2)`, not `|v|^(1/3)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates 3, 7-10:** Have `x/(c+v)^(1/3)` terms. Note `x/(c+v)^(1/3)` with c=0 gives `x/v^(1/3)` = `x*v^(-1/3)`, NOT `x*|v|^(1/3)`. These are different functions. Also, v takes both signs, so `v^(-1/3)` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates 4-5:** Have `x/(c+v)` — rational in v, can't produce `|v|^(1/3)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates 11-50:** Most have polynomial terms in v (like `v**4*x`, `v*x²`, `v*x⁴`). None of these can produce `x*|v|^(1/3)`. Let me check specific ones:

- **Candidate 34, 41, 47:** Have `v**c6` — this gives `v^c` but NOT `|v|^c`. Since v takes both signs, `v^(1/3)` is defined but equals `sign(v)*|v|^(1/3)`, which is NOT `|v|^(1/3)`. And this term isn't multiplied by x. [NO MATCH]

- **Candidates 22, 28-29, 32, 35:** Have `log(c*x+1)` or `exp(c*x)` — these are different basis functions entirely. [NO MATCH]

- **Candidate 36-37:** Have `x**c6` term. Setting c6=1 just gives another x term. Can't produce `|v|^(1/3)`. [NO MATCH]

For ALL candidates 1-50: None contain a term that can produce `x * |v|^(1/3)`. This is a required basis function in the GT that is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, logarithmic, and trigonometric basis functions present in the candidates.

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no candidate can match.
